SEMESTER S5 
 PUMP ENGINEERING AND HYDRAULIC CONTROL  
Course Code 
PEAGT522  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To equip students with the necessary knowledge and skills essential for addressing the dynamic 
challenges in the agricultural sector.  
2. To embark the students on a journey that spans from foundational principles to advanced 
concepts, preparing them for a future where sustainable and efficient water management in 
agriculture is paramount. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basic Principles of Fluid Mechanics-Introduction to Fluid Mechanics- 
Fundamentals of fluid properties. Types of flow: laminar, turbulent, and 
transitional- Bernoulli's equation and its relevance to pump systems. Flow in 
Pipes- Pipe friction losses and head calculations - Reynolds number and its 
significance - Hydraulic gradients in pump systems. Cavitation: causes, 
effects, and prevention- Net Positive Suction Head (NPSH) and its 
importance. Introduction to Pump Systems- Importance of pump systems in 
agriculture-Types of pumping systems in agriculture- Types of Pumps and 
Their Applications- Centrifugal pumps: working principles and applications 
- Positive displacement pumps: reciprocating and rotary pumps- Specialized 
 
9  

 
 
pumps for agricultural applications- Selection Criteria for Agricultural 
Pumps. 
2 
Introduction to Hydraulic Control Systems - Definition and significance of 
hydraulic control in agricultural machinery- Overview of hydraulic 
components: pumps, actuators, valves, and reservoirs- Hydraulic Symbols 
and Schematics- Control Valves and Their Types-Classification of Hydraulic 
Control Valves- Flow Control in Hydraulic Systems-Pressure Regulation in 
Hydraulic Systems. 
 
9  
3 
Pump Maintenance and Troubleshooting-Preventive Maintenance of Pumps 
and Hydraulic Systems - Preventive Maintenance Practices- Troubleshooting 
Common Issues in Pump Systems- Overhauling Hydraulic Components- 
Identifying and mitigating safety hazards in maintenance activities- Personal 
protective equipment (PPE) requirements. 
9  
4 
Strategies for Energy-Efficient Pumping- Pump system optimization for 
energy efficiency - Energy audit techniques  for pump systems - High-
efficiency pump designs  - Smart pump systems and their applications- 
Automation in Pump Control Systems- Programmable Logic Controllers 
(PLCs) in pump control- Remote sensing and monitoring of pump 
parameters- Sustainable pump technologies and eco-friendly materials- 
Anticipating and adapting to future developments. 
 
9

SEMESTER S5 
FUNDAMENTALS OF NANOSCIENCE 
Course Code 
PEAGT 523 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course is designed to provide a comprehensive understanding of organic 
semiconductors and action of various layers used in organic devices. 
2. The students will gain the skills necessary to design and develop organic devices like 
OLEDs, OFETs and OPVs after the completion of the course. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basics of Organic semiconductor, conduction mechanism in organic 
semiconductors, Pi and Sigma electron band theory. Fundamentals of 
conducting polymers. Charge transport in conjugated polymers. Effect of 
solitons. Conduction mechanism in doped polymeric semiconductors. 
Luminescence, injection and transports properties in organic semiconductors. 
9 
2 
Organic light emitting diodes(OLED) and Polymer light emitting diodes 
(PLED) – Basic device architecture, Single layer architecture and multilayer 
architecture, electrical properties and operating characteristics, Flexible 
display device architecture, Fabrication and characterization, Principle and 
architecture of organic transistors. 
9 
3 
Basic principle and architecture of Plastic Solar cell. Charge transport, effects 
of excitation diffusion, dissociation and luminescence, Photo-generation 
9 

 
 
process in organic heterojunction, photovoltaic cells. Processing of organic 
solar cells. Dye sensitization – dye sensitized solar cell. 
4 
Essential characteristics and conductivity of electrode materials in organo 
electronic devices, Effect of Indium Tin Oxide (ITO) oxidative properties on 
efficiency and shelf life of organic electronic devices, Buffer organic layer 
protection to the active layer. Doping and for increased efficiency and shelf 
life– architecture. 
Devices fabrication- Thin film coating technique. Spin coating, dip coating, 
doctor blading screen printing, inkjet printing, vapor deposition. R.F and 
microwave plasma assisted film coating. 
9

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 

 
 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

Course Objectives:

2. To Study the characteristics of fuels/Lubricates used in IC Engines.

8 
Determination of Flash Point and Fire Point of various fuels / lubricants 
9 
Thermal conductivity measurement using guarded plate apparatus. 
10 
Thermal conductivity measurement of pipe insulation using lagged pipe apparatus.

SEMESTER 6 
     AGRICULTURE ENGINEERING 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
SEMESTER S6 
POST HARVEST ENGINEERING OF CEREALS, OIL SEEDS AND 
HORTICULTURAL CROPS 
Course Code 
PCAGT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Unit Operations in 
Agricultural 
Processing
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provided fundamental knowledge in cereals, pulses and oilseeds processing 
2. To understand the performance evaluation of different types of cleaners, separators, and size 
reduction machines 
3. To learn various unit operations involved in processing of horticultural produce 
4. To learn preservation, packaging, storage and quality evaluation of   cereals, pulses oilseeds and 
horticultural products 
5. To enhance knowledge in operation of post-harvest equipment 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
FUNDAMENTALS OF POST HARVESTING 
Production and utilization of cereals and pulses, grain structure of major 
cereals, pulses and oilseeds and their milling fractions; grain quality 
standards and physico-chemical methods for evaluation of quality of flours. 
Cleaning and grading, aspiration, scalping; Size reduction: principle, Bond’s 
law, Kick’s law, Rittinger’s law, procedure (crushing, impact, cutting and 
shearing), Size reduction machinery: Jaw crusher, Hammer mill, Plate mill, 
Ball mill. 
 
11 

 
 
2 
PROCESSING OF CEREALS AND PULSES 
Pre-milling treatments and their effects on milling quality; parboiling and 
drying, Drying: moisture content and water activity; Free, bound and 
equilibrium 
moisture content, isotherm, 
hysteresis 
effect, EMC 
determination, Psychrometric chart and its use in drying, Drying principles 
and theory, Different methods of drying, conventional, modern and 
integrated rice milling operations; wheat roller flour milling; processes for 
milling of corn, oats, barley, gram, pulses, paddy and flour milling 
equipments. 
 
11 
3 
PROCESSING OF OILSEEDS 
Oilseed processing: mechanical expression, screw press, hydraulic press, 
solvent extraction methods, Extraction and refining of oil from coconut, soya 
bean, sunflower and rice bran. Packaging of processed products, design 
characteristics of milling equipments; selection, installation and their 
performance, BIS standards for various processed products 
11 
4 
PROCESSING OF HORTICULTURAL CROPS 
Importance of processing of fruits and vegetables, spices, condiments and 
flowers. Characteristics and properties of horticultural crops important for 
processing. Peeling, Slicing, Blanching, Chilling, freezing and Packaging.  
Cold storage heat load calculations and cold storage design, refrigerated 
vehicle and cold chain system. Dryers for fruits and vegetables, Osmo-
dehydration, General methods of preservation of fruits and vegetables, 
Flowcharts for preparation of different finished products, Important 
parameters and equipment used for different unit operations. 
 
11

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S6 
DAIRY AND FOOD ENGINEERING  
 
Course Code 
PCAGT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Food Processing and 
Preservation 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To expose the students to the fundamental knowledge of food, its properties and different 
methods of food processing  
2. To understand the chemical, physical, and biological properties of milk and dairy products 
3. To learn the methods and technologies used in the processing of milk and the production of 
various dairy products such as cheese, butter and ice cream. 
4. To gain knowledge about the design, operation, and maintenance of equipment and machinery 
used in the dairy and food industry, including pasteurizers, sterilizers, homogenizers, separators, 
evaporators, filtration and dryers. 
5. To equip the students to design and layout of dairy plant, sanitation and effluent treatment in 
dairy industry   
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
PROPERTIES AND PROCESSING OF MILK
Dairy Industry-importance and status; Diary development in India, Milk 
Types – Composition and thermal and chemical properties of milk and milk 
products, Production of high-quality milk, Method of raw milk procurement 
and preservation - Processing  
 
9 
2 
UNIT OPERATION IN MILK PROCESSING 
Process flow charts for product manufacture, Unit operation of various dairy 
 

 
 
and food processing systems. Principles and equipment related to receiving 
of milk, pasteurization, sterilization, homogenization, centrifugation and 
cream separation. 
9 
3 
PROCESSING AND PRESERVATION OF FOODS 
Evaporation: principles, types of evaporators, steam economy, multiple 
effect evaporation, multiple effect evaporation, vapour recompression. 
Principles of drying, spray drying, drum drying, freeze drying, Filtration: 
principle, types of filters; Membrane separation, RO, Nano-filtration, Ultra 
filtration and Macro-filtration, equipment and applications- Dairy plant 
design and layout-CIP, Dairy effluent treatment plant 
9 
4 
PROCESSING OF DAIRY PRODUCTS 
Manufacture of Milk Powder, Processing of Milk Products - Condensed Milk 
- Skim milk - Butter milk - Flavoured Milk, Whey, casein, yoghurt and 
paneer, Manufacture of Butter: principles, butter churn; Preparation methods 
and equipment for manufacture of Cheese, Ghee, ice creams and frozen 
desserts - standards for milk and milk products - Packaging of Milk and Milk 
Products 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
RENEWABLE ENERGY AND GREEN TECHNOLOGY   
 
Course Code 
PEAGT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the importance and role of renewable sources of energy in the energy sector  
 
2. To understand the production of energy through solar photovoltaic system 
3. To learn about wind energy and turbines 
4. To understand various aspects of bio energy and bio fuels 
5. To understand the characteristics and basic principle of green technology 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to energy- Classification-Energy and environment- Concept of 
Renewable Energy Sources (RES)-Clean Development Mechanism-Role of 
renewable energy for mitigation of Global warming. 
Solar Energy: Fundamentals and basic principles- Solar radiation 
measurement, Basic Principles of Solar thermal energy conversion, Flat 
plate and Concentrating collectors, different solar thermal devices, 
Applications, and gadgets- Solar drying, Solar still 
 
9 
2 
Solar Photo voltaic electricity production: Principles of Photo voltaic 
energy production-p-n junctions, Solar cells, PV Systems- Cell 
characteristics. 
Wind Energy: Energy available in wind, General formula, Lift and drag. 
 
9 

 
 
Basics of Wind energy conversion, Power coefficient- Betz limit-
Operational parameters of wind turbines-torque coefficient- tip speed ratio. 
Types of wind turbine rotors 
3 
Bio-energy: Thermo-chemical energy conversion of biomass – Biomass 
combustion- Combustion of Biomass and stoves -Biomass gasification, 
Types of gasifiers. Biochemical energy conversion of biomass: Anaerobic 
digestion process-types of biogas plants- Basic design aspects of Biogas 
plants- operational and environmental parameters affecting biogas 
generation.  Liquid bio-fuels, Basic principles for production of alcohol and 
biodiesel. 
Use of vegetable oils as fuel - Bio-diesel - general principles of the 
technology- production and use. Alcohol for fuel purpose- production 
processes and technology. Hydrogen as fuel – Hydrogen production by bio-
photolysis – Biogas Fuel cells 
9 
4 
Biomass combustion: Combustion, gasification and pyrolysis of biomass - 
Basic principles.  Technology and equipment for biomass combustion- 
Chemistry of gasification- Different types of gasifiers– Thermal 
applications of producer gas- Use of producer gas in engines 
Concept of Green Technology – Importance – Green fuels – Zero emissions 
target – Carbon credit and trading – Green energy production – Fuels cells 
and Biological Photovoltaics – Eco-friendly materials – Green building – 
Principles aspects Certification systems – Green Rating for Integrated 
Habitat Assessment (GRIHA) etc. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 

 
 
ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT 
Course Code 
PEAGT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarize the students, the concept of EIA and its development and need.  
2. To provide an awareness about administrative and legal measures for the protection of 
environment and environmental clearance procedures in India.   
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definition, Need for EIA, Evolution of EIA: Global & Indian scenario -
Environmental legislations in India- The Water (Prevention & Control of 
Pollution) Act 1974, The Air (Prevention & Control of Pollution) Act 1981, 
The Environmental (Protection) Act 1986- Environmental standards for 
water, air and noise quality- EIA Notification 1994 – EIA Revised 
notification 2006.  
 
9 
2 
Environmental clearance process in India: Screening, Scoping, Public 
Consultation, Appraisal- Form1-Category of projects- Generic structure of 
EIA report- Terms of Reference (ToR) -Types of EIA: strategic, regional, 
sectoral, project level- Rapid EIA and Comprehensive EIA- Initial 
Environmental Examination (IEE). 
 
9 
3 
EIA methodologies: Ad hoc, checklist, matrix, network and overlay- Impact 
Prediction, Evaluation and Mitigation-Prediction and assessment of the 
impact on water, air, and noise environment- assessment of ecological 
impacts and socio economic impacts. Impacts of modern agriculture and 
9 

 
 
deforestation on environment. 
4 
Environmental Management Plan (EMP): Goal and purpose- Importance of 
EMP- Content of an EMP- Role of environmental monitoring program. 
Environment Audit: need for audit- audit types and benefits- environmental 
audit procedure ISO 14001 standards: Importance, salient features - Stages in 
implementation- Benefits. EIA case studies (Indian) - a hydroelectric project, 
a agricultural production unit, food processing, fertilizer unit, irrigation 
project. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
FOOD QUALITY & SAFETY 
Course Code 
PEAGT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarize the students, the concept of EIA and its development and need.  
2. To provide an awareness about administrative and legal measures for the protection of 
environment and environmental clearance procedures in India.   
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Food hygiene – introduction, definition, basic aspects of personal hygiene, 
disease transmission - food handling -preventing food borne illnesses, 
education of food handler in handling and serving food, importance of 
personal hygiene of the food handler, pest control - food institutions – 
sanitation of food institutions.  
 
9 
2 
Food packaging – definition, functions, classification, laws related to 
packaging. Food labeling: standards, purpose, description types of labels, 
labeling regulation barcode, nutrition labeling – nutrition labeling, health 
claims, and mandatory labeling provision.  
 
9 
3 
Food adulteration – definition of adulteration, adulterants, types of adulterants, 
food laws – essential commodities act, milk and milk products order, food 
standardisation and regulation agencies in India- agencies at state level, central 
food laboratories, HACCP, powers of food inspectors. Food spoilage -
9 

 
 
physical, chemical and microbiological spoilage of foods. Conduct a hazard 
analysis, CCP identification, establish critical limits for each CCP, establish 
CCP monitoring procedures, establish corrective actions procedures, establish 
procedures for HACCP verification and validation, documenting the HACCP 
Program.  
4 
Introduction to food preservation- methods of preservation, general 
principles and applications of food preservation. Preservation by use of 
temperature - preservation by use of high and low temperature. Preservation 
by drying- preservation by drying and use of salt and sugar - enhancement of 
foods – food fortification, enrichment, supplementation, fermentation, 
germination, pre- and probiotics and organic foods.  
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
DESIGN OF AGRICULTURAL IMPLEMENTS & MACHINES 
 
Course Code 
PBAGT604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Farm Machinery and 
Equipment 
Tractor systems and 
control
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the basic concept of machine design. 
2. To understand the strength and stress failures of different joints.  
3. To learn the design of shaft, keys, belts and gears. 
4. To understand the design considerations of tillage implements. 
5. To understand the design considerations of sowing, harvesting and threshing equipment / machines 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Understanding of design concepts, Phases of design, design considerations. 
Common engineering materials and their mechanical properties. Types of 
loads and stresses, Failure theories, factor of safety, selection of allowable 
stress. Stress concentration. Elementary fatigue and creep aspects. Cotter 
joints, knuckle joint and pinned joints, turnbuckle. Design of welded joints 
subjected to static loads. 
 
9  
2 
Design of threaded fasteners subjected to direct static loads, bolted joints 
loaded in shear and bolted joints subjected to eccentric loading. Design of 
shafts under torsion and combined bending and torsion. Design of keys. 
Design of lever, Design of Jaw coupling, sleeve, and rigid flange couplings. 
Design of helical and leaf springs. Design of flat belt and V-belt drives and 
pulleys. 
 
9  

 
 
3 
Design of gears- Spur gear, Design of screw motion mechanisms like screw 
jack, lead screw, etc. Selection of anti-friction bearings -Ball bearings  
Design considerations for tillage implements such as ploughs, harrows and 
cultivators. Design of mould board plough, analysis of forces acting on 
plough bottom by the cut soil slices,  
Disc implement types and design of disc for different disc tools, spacing of 
disc in multi-disc tools. Force analysis of vertical and inclined disc tools. 
Specific work of rotary tools and machine and dynamic forces. Reliability 
criteria in design and its application. 
9 
4 
Design consideration of sowing and planting equipment, design of seed 
metering mechanism, design parameters of seed and fertilizer box and frame, 
design of seed metering mechanism of planters. Fertilizers handling 
equipment and their design parameters and requirements. 
Design consideration of threshing and harvesting equipment with reference to 
types of cylinder and safety measures. 
Design and selection of matching power unit. Safety devices and ergonomical 
considerations for the design and development of tractors & farm implements.
 
9 
 
Suggestion on Project Topics 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 60 marks, ESE: 40 marks)

SEMESTER S6 
PLASTIC APPLICATION IN AGRICULTURE   
Course Code 
OEAGT611 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand about sustainability in agricultural processes, promoting improved yields 
and resource conservation. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Types and quality of plastics used in soil and water conservation, production 
agriculture and post-harvest management. Quality control measures. Bore-
well casing and subsurface drainage. Drip and sprinkler irrigation systems. 
Use of polymers in control of percolation losses in fields. Soil conditioning - 
soil solarisation, effects of different colour plastic mulching in surface 
covered cultivation. Nursery management - Use of plastics in nursery raising, 
nursery bags, trays etc. 
 
9 
2 
Plastics as cladding material, green / poly / shade net houses, wind breaks, 
poly tunnels and crop covers. Plastic nets for crop protection - anti insect 
nets, bird protection nets. Plastic fencing. Plastics in drying, preservation, 
handling and storage of agricultural produce, innovative plastic packaging 
solutions for processed food products. Plastic cap covers for storage of food 
grains in open. 
 
9 
3 
Use of plastics as alternate material for manufacturing farm equipment and 
machinery. Plastics for aquacultural engineering and animal husbandry - 
9 

 
 
animal shelters, vermi-beds and inland fisheries. Silage film technique for 
fodder preservation. Agencies involved in the promotion of plasticulture in 
agriculture at national and state level. Human resource development in 
plasticutlure applications. 
4 
Water management - use of plastics in in-situ moisture conservation and rain 
water harvesting. Plastic film lining in canal, pond and reservoir. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
LANDSCAPE DESIGN AND MANGEMENT 
 
Course Code 
OEAGT612  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To equip students to create visually appealing, ecologically conscious outdoor spaces and 
fosters skills applicable to various fields such as architecture in agriculture, urban 
planning, and environmental science. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Standards, Bye laws and planning regulations applicable to building and 
landscape development. The role of statutory and regulatory bodies such as 
the Municipal Corporation, N.D.M.C, D.D.A and Urban Art commission etc. 
Implementation process Sequence of activities from inception to completion: 
agencies involved at each stage, their professional relationships, and 
obligations. Co-ordination of agencies and activities on site. Practical 
examples. 
 
9 
2 
Contract Procedure; Criteria for selecting contractors: the process of calling 
tenders. Comparison of various kind of tenders with regard to objectives, 
utility, and appropriateness. Tender Documentation and evaluation of tender; 
negotiations with contractors. Contract Documentation: Forms of contract; 
General and special conditions, specifications, Bill of quantities; significant 
 
9 

 
 
clauses pertaining to defects, maintenance, arbitrations, etc. Parties to the 
contract; their roles, contractual relationships, and legal obligations.  
3 
Preparation of a maintenance plan: watering, fertilization, aeration, mulching, 
edging, pest control, pruning, and weed control. Design for irrigation, 
drainage, electrical etc, Methods and materials involved in maintenance of the 
landscape features. Maintenance bids and services involved. 
9 
4 
Progress evaluation and monitoring: various kinds of estimates, review and 
updating, simple examples of pert charts and bar diagrams. Site 
documentation: importance of written records. Site instruction book, periodic 
reports, visual records, bar charts etc. Techniques of inspection and quality 
control; visits to site under development. 
 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
 UNIT OPERATIONS IN AGRICULTURAL PROCESSING 
 
Course Code 
PCAGL607 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks   
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the various unit operations in cereals, pulses, fruits and oil seed processing 
industries 
2. To gain practical experience and proficiency in using various machineries involved in post-
harvest unit operations  
3. To develop practical skills in operation and performance evaluation of fruit processing 
machineries 
4. To develop technical skills on performance evaluation cleaning, separating and milling 
equipment 
5. To gain sufficient knowledge on drying characteristics of grains and measurement of moisture 
content and EMC  
Expt.  
No.

1 
Performance evaluation of different types of cleaners and separators 
2 
Performance evaluation of different size reduction machines 
3 
Determination of fineness modulus and uniformity index 
4 
Measurement of moisture content of grains: dry basis and wet basis

OUxD4713C7QCh&si=iqXbDAJr840PL058 
3 
https://youtube.com/playlist?list=PLhWyf911na-XNr-totysuQubXQLXlt6BN&si=D-
qOw8w2XUdLV3zr 
 
Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 

 
 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 

 
 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S7 
WATERSHED DEVELOPMENT AND MANAGEMENT 
 
Course Code 
PGAET741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The student will get a comprehensive idea about watershed management.  
2. The student will be capable of planning and execution of watershed management projects. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Watershed - introduction and characteristics. Watershed development - 
problems and prospects, investigation, topographical survey, soil characteristics, 
vegetative cover, land use practices and socio-economic factors. Watershed 
management - concept, objectives, factors affecting, watershed planning based 
on land capability classes, hydrologic data for watershed planning, watershed 
codification, delineation and prioritization of watersheds – sediment yield index. 
Water budgeting in a watershed. 
 
9 
2 
Management measures - rainwater conservation technologies - in-situ and ex-
situ storage, water harvesting and recycling. Dry farming techniques - inter-
terrace and inter-bund land management. Integrated watershed management - 
concept, components, arable lands – agriculture and horticulture, non-arable 
lands - forestry, fishery and animal husbandry. 
 
9 

 
 
3 
Effect of cropping systems, land management and cultural practices on 
watershed hydrology. Watershed programme - execution, follow-up practices, 
maintenance, monitoring and evaluation. Participatory watershed management - 
role of watershed associations, user groups and self-help groups. People’s 
participation in watershed management. 
9 
4 
Estimate preparation for watershed projects- Detailed estimate-Analysis of 
rates-Abstract of estimate. Planning and formulation of project proposal for 
watershed management programme including cost-benefit analysis. Preparation 
of detailed project report (DPR) for watershed projects. 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
POST HARVEST ENGINEERING OF HORTICULTURAL CROPS   
Course Code 
PEAGT742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To acquaint and equip the students with processing and handling of fruits and vegetables and 
flowers 
2. To minimize the post-harvest losses through value addition and post-harvest unit operations 
3. To facilitate the design features of the equipment used for the processing of horticultural products 
4. To understand various preservation, packaging and storage methods of horticultural produce 
5. To expose the students to modern facilities in supply chain management of horticultural products 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Status-Importance, constituents of fruits and vegetables, Post harvest losses in 
fruits and vegetables, factors influencing losses, Enzymatic and textural 
changes during ripening.Engineering properties of horticultural crops. –. Post har
vegetables, spices, condiments and flowers, Characteristics and properties of 
horticultural crops important for processing, Peeling: Differentpeeling methods 
and devices (manual peeling, mechanical peeling, chemical peeling, and 
thermalpeeling), Slicing of horticultural crops: equipment for slicing, 
shredding, crushing, chopping,juice extraction, etc., Blanching: Importance and 
objectives; blanching methods, effects on food(nutrition, colour, pigment, 
 
9 

 
 
texture). 
 
2 
Chilling and freezing: Application of refrigeration in different 
perishable food products, Thermophilic, mesophilic &Psychrophilic micro-
organisms, Chillingrequirements of different fruits and vegetables, Freezing of 
food, freezing time calculations,slow and fast freezing, Equipment for chilling 
and freezing (mechanical & cryogenic), Effect onfood during chilling and 
freezing, 
Cold 
storage 
heat 
load 
calculations 
and 
cold 
storage 
design,refrigerated vehicle and cold chain system, Dryers for fruits and 
vegetables: tray, drum, spray, pneumatic, fluidized bed dryer, and foam mat 
drying. Osmo-dehydration, freeze drying. Irradiation, surface coatings, 
chemical dips, preservatives. 
 
9 
3 
Packaging of horticultural commodities, Packaging requirements (in terms of 
light transmittance, heat, moisture and gas proof, microorganisms.  Different 
types of packaging materials commonly used for raw and processed fruits and 
vegetables products, bulk and retail packages and packaging machines, 
handling and transportation of fruits and vegetables, Packhouse technology, 
Minimal processing 
Ethylene evolution during storage, methods to prevent ethylene production, 
physiological loss of weight, methods of storage, Low temperature storage, 
evaporative cooled storage, controlled atmospheric storage, Modified 
atmospheric packaging. Pests, insects, rodents, fungi – their nature, occurrence 
and control. Modern techniques of infestation control. Application of quality 
control techniques. 
9 
4 
Preservation Technology, General methods of preservation of fruits and 
vegetables, Brief description and advantages and disadvantages of different 
physical/ chemical and other methods of preservation, Flowcharts for 
preparation of different finished products, Important parameters and equipment 
used for different unit operations, Post harvest management and equipment for 
spices and flowers, Quality control in fruit and vegetable processing industry. 
Food supply chain. 
 
9

Course Objectives:

concepts. 
2. To develop analytical and practical skills in farm machinery and implements. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to mechanics of tillage tools, engineering properties of soil, 
principles and concepts, stress strain relationship. 
 
9 
2 
Design of tillage tools principles of soil cutting, design equation, force 
analysis, assessment of the dynamic properties of soils. 
9 
3 
Application of dimensional analysis in soil dynamics and traction prediction 
equation, Methods of dimensional analysis, Development of prediction 
equations. 
9 
4 
Introduction to traction and mechanics, off road traction and mobility, traction 
model, traction improvement, tyre size, tyre lug geometry and their effects, tyre 
testing. Soil compaction and plant growth, variability and application of GIS in 
soil dynamics. 
9

Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Size reduction: Benefits, classification, determination and designation of the 
fineness of ground material, sieve/screen analysis,  fineness modulus and 
uniformity index,  principle and mechanisms of comminution of food, 
Rittinger’s, Kick’s and Bond’s equations, work index, energy utilization; Size 
reduction equipment: Principle, types, crushers (jaw crushers, gyratory, smooth 
roll), hammer mills and impactors, attrition mills, burr mill, tumbling mills, ultra 
fine grinders, fluid jet pulverizer, colloid mill, cutting machines (slicing, dicing, 
shredding, pulping). 
 
9 
2 
Drying: principle, moisture and its removal, utilities of drying, Moisture content 
and its measurements, Moisture content representation, Determination methods: 
 

 
 
direct and indirect methods, Equilibrium moisture content (EMC), Method for 
determination of EMC: dynamic methods and static methods, Drying theory, 
methods of drying, drying rate periods, Mechanical drying types; thin layer 
drying and deep bed drying 
9 
3 
Rice milling, parboiling, methods:traditional and modern methods, milling 
equipments, hullers, sheller, paddy separator, removal of bran, polisher, glazing, 
grading , milling efficiency, Pulse milling, unit operations, commercial scale 
methods (wet milling and dry milling, Jabalpur method, CFTRI method, 
Pantnagar process, CIAE method), milling efficiency,  Milling of oilseeds: 
mechanical expression, screw press, hydraulic press, solvent extraction methods, 
preconditioning of oilseeds, refining of oil 
9 
4 
Importance of processing of fruits and vegetables. Peeling: Different peeling 
methods and devices (manual peeling, mechanical peeling, chemical peeling, 
and thermal peeling), Slicing of horticultural crops: equipment for slicing, 
shredding, crushing, chopping, juice extraction, etc., Blanching: Importance and 
objectives; blanching methods, effects on food (nutrition, colour, pigment, 
texture), Physiological changes during ripening, maturity index, firmness, sugar 
acid ratio, respiration, pre-cooling 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
WASTE AND BYPRODUCTS UTILIZATION  
Course Code 
PGAET753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To acquaint and equip the students with the techniques of utilization of agricultural waste and by-
products and also about development of value-added products from wastes. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Conversion processes: Thermo-chemical conversions, densification, combustion 
and gasification, extraction, biological conversions, anaerobic digestion, 
biochemical digestion process, digestion systems, energy from anaerobic 
digestion, cellulose degradation, fermentation process. Agricultural wastes as 
paper, boards and fuel. 
 
9 
2 
Briquetting: Briquetted fuel from husk, hull and other wastes selection, design 
of briquetting machines. Utilization of shell, stem and stalk: Production of 
activated carbon. By-products of agro-industries: Rice mill, oil mill, cattle feed 
mill, valuable constituents and composition. Utilization of rice husk: Production 
of silica and cement from rice husk. Stabilization and storage of rice bran, 
extraction of rice bran oil. 
 
9 
3 
By-products of oil refining: Fatty acids/soap stock, wax and gum, characteristics 
and utilization. Rice germ and broken rice. Production of starch and infant food, 
industrial uses of starch. By-products of oil milling: Oil cake and defatted oil 
9 

 
 
cake, cattle feed and industrial uses. Utilization of starch and other industrial 
wastes: Microcrystalline cellulose, production of ethanol, wastes of tapioca 
starch industries, Tapioca thippi-utilization as fuel, extraction of starch by 
hydrolysis, utilization of starch for food, adhesives and feed purposes. 
4 
By-products of sugar industry: Sugarcane tops, bagasse, molasses and press-
mud, utilization as animal feed. By-products of fruits and vegetables-based 
agro-industries: Mango seed kernel and pineapple waste. 
 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To gain a comprehensive understanding of the principals involved in creating controlled 
environments for plant growth, fostering skills in architectural planning, climate control, 
and sustainable cultivation practices. 
SYLLABUS 
Module No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
History and types of greenhouses; importance, function, and features of 
green house; scope and development of greenhouse technology. Location, 
Planning, and various component of greenhouse; design criteria and 
calculation; constructional material and methods of construction; covering 
materials and its characteristics, solar heat transfer, solar fraction for green 
house, steady state analysis of green house. 
9 
2 
Greenhouse heating, cooling, shedding and ventilation systems; Carbon 
Dioxide generation and monitoring and lighting systems, instrumentation 
& computerized environmental Control Systems. 
9 
3 
Watering, fertilization, root substrate and its pasteurization, containers and 
benches, plant nutrition. Alternative cropping systems; plant tissue culture, 
chemical growth regulation; disease control; integrated pest management; 
postproduction quality and handling. 
9 

 
 
4 
Cost analysis of greenhouse production; Applications of green house & its 
repair & maintenance

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To enable the students to typically revolve around optimizing agricultural and related business 
operations to achieve sustainable growth, profitability, and social responsibility. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact Hours 
1 
Agri-business - scope, characteristics, types. Management - importance, 
definition, management and administration, management thoughts, 
Small business - characteristics and stages of growth.  Principles, forms 
of agri-business organizations, staffing, directing, supervision and 
motivation. Controlling - types, performance evaluation and control 
techniques. Management approaches - Profit Centered Approach, 
Management by objectives and Quality Circles. Strength, Weakness, 
Opportunities and Threat (SWOT) Analysis. 
9 
2 
Functional areas of Agri-business - Production and Operations 
management - functions, planning physical facilities and managing 
quality. Agro-inputs and products inventory management – raw 
material procurement, inventory types, and costs. Marketing 
management- Marketing environment, marketing mix - Agricultural 
input marketing firms. 
9 
3 
Forms of agri-business organizations - Role of lead bank in 
9 

 
 
agribusiness finance - Financial management. Acquiring capital- 
Budget analysis. Concepts and determinants- Business project 
scheduling of raw material procurement - production management - 
launching products (branding, placement) - Input marketing promotion 
activities. 
4 
Agricultural products - marketing promotion activities - product pricing 
methods. District Industries Centre - Consumer survey - Agricultural 
inputs retailing - Market potential assessment - types of distribution 
channels - Return on Investment - Personnel management. Recruitment, 
selection and training - Technology in Agri Business. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
 SENSORS, AI AND ROBOTICS IN PRECISION AGRICULTURE 
 
Course Code 
PEAGT861  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart basic knowledge on the modern technologies that are used for precision farming and 
their applications 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to sensors, sensors in precision farming; Spectral based sensors; 
Development of sensors and controls; Image analysis technology; Crop yield 
monitors; Yield Monitors: Components, Differential GPS Receiver, GNSS 
Receiver, mass flow sensors. Impact plates, measuring volume with a 
photoelectric sensor, volumetric flow sensing and alternatives. Grain 
moisture sensor, fan speed sensor, elevator speed sensor, header position, 
yield monitor data, cotton yield monitors 
 
9  
2 
Introduction Remote sensing for precision agriculture and applications for 
crop monitoring, Developments in livestock and building control: Radio 
telemetry systems to remotely monitor and record physiological parameters. 
 
9  
3 
Global navigation satellite system (GNNS). Satellite ranging: Accuracy, 
standards, components of GIS, data layers, map component, attribute table 
9 

 
 
component, Function of a GIS, resolution. Data formats: Vector or raster. 
GIS for precision farming, data analysis, field calculator, convert to grid, 
interpolation, reclassification, image classification, band math, interpretation 
of analysis, farm management information systems, and crop intelligence 
4 
Introduction to robotics in agriculture, Concept of robotics and classification 
and components, Applications of robotics in automation of farm operations, 
sensors and actuators, control electronics, Algorithms and programming for 
microcontroller and microprocessor-based robots, telemetry, remote control 
and autonomous operation of agricultural robots. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
DEVELOPMENT OF PROCESSED FOOD PRODUCTS  
 
Course Code 
PEAGT862 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the transformation of raw materials into consumables.  
2. To learn the fundamentals of innovative techniques, technological advancements and culinary 
expertise in modern food industries. 
3. To provide the knowledge and skills needed to meet the dynamic demands of the food industry 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Applications of unit operations to the food industry, analytical processing 
concepts with regards to mass and energy balances, equipment involved in the 
commercially important food processing methods and unit operations; value 
addition to cereals like rice and wheat. 
 
9  
2 
Parboiling of rice, quality of processed products of rice & wheat. Processing 
of pulses, spices, and condiments; extruded food product, fermented food 
product, frozen and dried product, technology of meat, fish and poultry 
products, technology of milk and milk products.  
 
9  

 
 
3 
Technology of oilseeds and fat products, snack foods, Fruits, and vegetables 
product: candy, nutraceuticals, food product development trends, food 
additives and labeling.  
9 
4 
Process equipment for thermal processing evaporation, dehydration, drying, 
blenching, pasteurization, distillation. Mechanical separation filtration, 
sieving, centrifugation, sedimentation; mechanical handling-conveying and 
elevation; size reduction and classification-mixing; kneading, blending. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
FOOD PACKAGING TECHNOLOGY  
 
Course Code 
PEAGT863 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand about packaging methods and the properties of packaging materials. 
2. To understand the different packaging materials used in food industry, packaging machineries, 
modern packaging techniques etc. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction of storage: Factors affecting shelf life of food material during 
storage, Spoilage mechanism during storage, Definition, Requirement, 
Importance and scope of packaging of foods. 
 
9  
2 
Introduction of packaging: Types and classification of packaging system, 
Advantage of modern packaging system, Different types of packaging 
materials used. Types of packaging: Different forms of packaging, metal 
container, Glass container, Plastic container, Flexible films, Shrink packaging, 
Vacuum and gas packaging. Modified and Controlled atmospheric packaging 
(MAP and CAP), Active and Intelligent Packaging, Aseptic Packaging. 
 
9  

 
 
3 
Selection of packaging material: Packaging requirement and their selection for 
the raw and processed foods, Advantages and disadvantages of these 
packaging materials, Effect of these materials on packed commodities, 
Package testing, Printing, Labelling and lamination. Flexible Packaging: 
Moulding – Injection, blow, extrusion methods Package Testing: Functional 
and Mechanical tests Packaging and filling systems. 
9 
4 
Economics of packaging: Economics of packaging, Performance evaluation 
of different methods of packaging food products, Their merits and demerits, 
Scope for improvements, Disposal and recycle of packaging waste. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
MECHATRONICS   
 
Course Code 
PEAGT864 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the cutting-edge field of Mechatronics with a specialized focus on its applications 
in agriculture.  
2. To learn the integration of mechanical systems, electronics, computer science, and control 
engineering is revolutionizing farming practices.  
3. To understand how mechatronics is enhancing efficiency, sustainability, and precision in modern 
agriculture, paving the way for innovative solutions to address the challenges of the agricultural 
industry. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Mechatronics and Sensors in Agriculture-Introduction to 
Mechatronics-Basic Electronics and Electrical Components- Sensors and 
Actuators in Agricultural Systems-Signal Conditioning and Processing-
Introduction to Microcontrollers and Microprocessors-Applications of 
Mechatronics in Agriculture. Control Systems in Agricultural Machinery- 
Introduction to Control Systems- Feedback Control Systems-PID Controllers 
 
9  

 
 
in 
Agricultural 
Machinery-PLC 
(Programmable 
Logic 
Controller) 
Applications 
2 
Modeling and Simulation of Agricultural Systems-Precision Farming and 
Automated Control. Robotics in Agriculture-Introduction to Agricultural 
Robotics- Types of Agricultural Robots- Robotic Vision Systems in 
Agriculture- Robot Manipulators and Grippers- Autonomous Navigation in 
Agricultural Robotics-Precision Agriculture using Robotics. 
 
9  
3 
Data Analytics and Decision Support in Precision Agriculture- Introduction to 
Precision Agriculture- Data Acquisition and Management in Agriculture-Data 
Analytics Techniques for Crop Monitoring- GIS (Geographic Information 
System) in Agriculture-Decision Support Systems in Precision Agriculture- 
Case Studies in Precision Agriculture. 
9 
4 
Emerging Trends in Mechatronics for Agriculture-Internet of Things 
(IoT) in Agriculture-Artificial Intelligence in Agricultural Systems-
Drones and Unmanned Aerial Vehicles (UAVs) in Agriculture- 
Sustainable Agriculture Technologies- Future Prospects and Challenges 
in Agricultural Mechatronics. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
HUMAN ENGG AND SAFETY 
Course Code 
OEAGT831  
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart the fundamental knowledge to the student on the importance of human 
engineering and safety in the field of agriculture machinery. 
2. To gain a general understanding of the safety features and regulation acts in farm 
machinery. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Human factors in system development, Concept of systems; basic processes 
in system development, performance reliability. Human performance. 
Information input process, visual displays, major types and use of displays, 
auditory and factual displays. Speech communications. 
 
9  
2 
Biomechanics of motion, types of movements, Range of movements, Strength 
and endurance, speed and accuracy, human control of systems. Human motor 
activities, controls, tools and related devices.  
 
9  

 
 
3 
Anthropometry: arrangement and utilization of work space, atmospheric 
conditions, heat exchange process and performance, air pollution.  
9  
4 
Dangerous machine (Regulation) act, Rehabilitation and compensation to 
accident victims, Safety gadgets for spraying, threshing, Chaff cutting and 
tractor & trailer operation etc.  
 
9
